183→//\n   184→// waitForPriorityQueue implements heap.Interface. The item occurring next in\n   185→// time (i.e., the item with the smallest readyAt) is at the root (index 0).\n   186→// Peek returns this minimum item at index 0. {\n\tTypedInterface[T]\n\n\t// clock tracks time for delayed firing\n\tclock clock.Clock\n\n\t// stopCh lets us signal a shutdown to the waiting loop\n\tstopCh chan struct{}\n\t// stopOnce guarantees we only signal shutdown a single time\n\tstopOnce sync.Once\n\n\t// heartbeat ensures we wait no more than maxWait before firing\n\theartbeat clock.Ticker\n\n\t// waitingForAddCh is a buffered channel that feeds waitingForAdd\n\twaitingForAddCh chan *waitFor[T]\n\n\t// metrics counts the number of retries\n\tmetrics retryMetrics\n}\n\n// waitFor holds the data to add and the time it should be added\ntype waitFor[T any] struct {\n\tdata    T\n\treadyAt time.Time\n\t// index in the priority queue (heap)\n\tindex int\n}\n\n// waitForPriorityQueue implements a priority queue for waitFor items.\n//\n// waitForPriorityQueue implements heap.Interface. The item occurring next in\n// time (i.e., the item with the smallest readyAt) is at the root (index 0).\n// Peek returns this minimum item at index 0. Pop returns the minimum item after\n// it has been removed from the queue and placed at index Len()-1 by\n// container/heap. Push adds an item at index Len(), and container/heap\n// percolates it into the correct location.\ntype waitForPriorityQueue[T any] []*waitFor[T]\n\nfunc (pq waitForPriorityQueue[T]) Len() int {\n\treturn len(pq)\n}\nfunc (pq waitForPriorityQueue[T]) Less(i, j int) bool {\n\treturn pq[i].readyAt.Before(pq[j].readyAt)\n}\nfunc (pq waitForPriorityQueue[T]) Swap(i, j int) {\n\tpq[i], pq[j] = pq[j], pq[i]\n\tpq[i].index = i\n\tpq[j].index = j\n}\n\n// Push adds an item to the queue. Push should not be called directly; instead,\n// use `heap.Push`.\nfunc (pq *waitForPriorityQueue[T]) Push(x interface{}) {\n\tn := len(*pq)\n\titem := x.(*waitFor[T])\n\titem.index = n\n\t*pq = append(*pq, item)\n}\n\n// Pop removes an item from the queue. Pop should not be called directly;\n// instead, use `heap.Pop`.\nfunc (pq *waitForPriorityQueue[T]) Pop() interface{} {\n\tn := len(*pq)\n\titem := (*pq)[n-1]\n\titem.index = -1\n\t*pq = (*pq)[0:(n - 1)]\n\treturn item\n}\n\n// Peek returns the item at the beginning of the queue, without removing the\n// item or otherwise mutating the queue. It is safe to call directly.\nfunc (pq waitForPriorityQueue[T]) Peek() interface{} {\n\treturn pq[0]\n}\n\n// ShutDown stops the queue. After the queue drains, the returned shutdown bool\n// on Get() will be true. This method may be invoked more than once.\nfunc (q *delayingType[T]) ShutDown() {\n\tq.stopOnce.Do(func() {\n\t\tq.TypedInterface.ShutDown()\n\t\tclose(q.stopCh)\n\t\tq.heartbeat.Stop()\n\t})\n}\n\n// AddAfter adds the given item to the work queue after the given delay\nfunc (q *delayingType[T]) AddAfter(item T, duration time.Duration) {\n\t// don't add if we're already shutting down\n\tif q.ShuttingDown() {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tq.metrics.retry()\n\n\t// immediately add things with no delay\n\tif duration <= 0 {\n\t\tq.Add(item)\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tselect {\n\tcase <-q.stopCh:\n\t\t// unblock if ShutDown() is called\n\tcase q.waitingForAddCh <- &waitFor[T]{data: item, readyAt: q.clock.Now().Add(duration)}:\n\t}\n}\n\n// maxWait keeps a max bound on the wait time. It's just insurance against weird things happening.\n// Checking the queue every 10 seconds isn't expensive and we know that we'll never end up with an\n// expired item sitting for more than 10 seconds.\nconst maxWait = 10 * time.Second\n\n// waitingLoop runs until the workqueue is shutdown and keeps a check on the list of items to be added.\nfunc (q *delayingType[T]) waitingLoop() {\n\tdefer utilruntime.HandleCrash()\n\n\t// Make a placeholder channel to use when there are no items in our list\n\tnever := make(<-chan time.Time)\n\n\t// Make a timer that expires when the item at the head of the waiting queue is ready\n\tvar nextReadyAtTimer clock.Timer\n\n\twaitingForQueue := &waitForPriorityQueue[T]{}\n\theap.Init(waitingForQueue)\n\n\twaitingEntryByData := map[T]*waitFor[T]{}\n\n\tfor {\n\t\tif q.TypedInterface.ShuttingDown() {\n\t\t\treturn\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tnow := q.clock.Now()\n\n\t\t// Add ready entries\n\t\tfor waitingForQueue.Len() > 0 {\n\t\t\tentry := waitingForQueue.Peek().(*waitFor[T])\n\t\t\tif entry.readyAt.After(now) {\n\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tentry = heap.Pop(waitingForQueue).(*waitFor[T])\n\t\t\tq.Add(entry.data)\n\t\t\tdelete(waitingEntryByData, entry.data)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Set up a wait for the first item's readyAt (if one exists)\n\t\tnextReadyAt := never\n\t\tif waitingForQueue.Len() > 0 {\n\t\t\tif nextReadyAtTimer != nil {\n\t\t\t\tnextReadyAtTimer.Stop()\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tentry := waitingForQueue.Peek().(*waitFor[T])\n\t\t\tnextReadyAtTimer = q.clock.NewTimer(entry.readyAt.Sub(now))\n\t\t\tnextReadyAt = nextReadyAtTimer.C()\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase <-q.stopCh:\n\t\t\treturn\n\n\t\tcase <-q.heartbeat.C():\n\t\t\t// continue the loop, which will add ready items\n\n\t\tcase <-nextReadyAt:\n\t\t\t// continue the loop, which will add ready items\n\n\t\tcase waitEntry := <-q.waitingForAddCh:\n\t\t\tif waitEntry.readyAt.After(q.clock.Now()) {\n\t\t\t\tinsert(waitingForQueue, waitingEntryByData, waitEntry)\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\tq.Add(waitEntry.data)\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tdrained := false\n\t\t\tfor !drained {\n\t\t\t\tselect {\n\t\t\t\tcase waitEntry := <-q.waitingForAddCh:\n\t\t\t\t\tif waitEntry.readyAt.After(q.clock.Now()) {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tinsert(waitingForQueue, waitingEntryByData, waitEntry)\n\t\t\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tq.Add(waitEntry.data)\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\t\t\tdrained = true\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// insert adds the entry to the priority queue, or updates the readyAt if it already exists in the queue\nfunc insert[T comparable](q *waitForPriorityQueue[T], knownEntries map[T]*waitFor[T], entry *waitFor[T]) {\n\t// if the entry already exists, update the time only if it would cause the item to be queued sooner\n\texisting, exists := knownEntries[entry.data]\n\tif exists {\n\t\tif existing.readyAt.After(entry.readyAt) {\n\t\t\texisting.readyAt = entry.readyAt\n\t\t\theap.Fix(q, existing.index)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\theap.Push(q, entry)\n\tknownEntries[entry.data] = entry\n}\n","numLines":361,"startLine":1,"totalLines":361}}}

34→\t\"k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue\"\n    35→)\n    36→\n    37→// Controller demonstrates how to implement a controller with client-go.\n    38→type Controller struct {\n    39→\tindexer  cache.Indexer\n    40→\tqueue    workqueue.TypedRateLimitingInterface[string]\n    41→\tinformer cache.Controller\n    42→}\n    43→\n    44→// NewController creates a new Controller.\n    45→func NewController(queue workqueue.TypedRateLimitingInterface[string], indexer cache.Indexer, informer cache.Controller) *Controller {\n    46→\treturn &Controller{\n    47→\t\tinformer: informer,\n    48→\t\tindexer:  indexer,\n    49→\t\tqueue:    queue,\n    50→\t}\n    51→}\n    52→\n    53→func (c *Controller) processNextItem() bool {\n    54→\t// Wait until there is a new item in the working queue\n    55→\tkey, quit := c.queue.Get()\n    56→\tif quit {\n    57→\t\treturn false\n    58→\t}\n    59→\t// Tell the queue that we are done with processing this key. This unblocks the key for other workers\n    60→\t// This allows safe parallel processing because two pods with the same key are never processed in\n    61→\t// parallel.\n    62→\tdefer c.queue.Done(key)\n    63→\n    64→\t// Invoke the method containing the business logic\n    65→\terr := c.syncToStdout(key)\n    66→\t// Handle the error if something went wrong during the execution of the business logic\n    67→\tc.handleErr(err, key)\n    68→\treturn true\n    69→}\n    70→\n    71→// syncToStdout is the business logic of the controller. In this controller it simply prints\n    72→// information about the pod to stdout. The core implementation is located in staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/, which is mirrored in the client-go--v0.32.0 repository.\\n\\n**Core Interfaces and Implementations:**\\n\\n1. **RateLimitingInterface** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/rate_limiting_queue.go):\\n   - Defines TypedRateLimitingInterface[T] which extends TypedDelayingInterface[T]\\n   - Key methods: AddRateLimited(item T), Forget(item T), NumRequeues(item T)\\n   - Implementation: rateLimitingType[T] struct wraps a TypedDelayingInterface and a TypedRateLimiter\\n   - Factory functions: NewRateLimitingQueue, NewTypedRateLimitingQueue, NewTypedRateLimitingQueueWithConfig\\n\\n2. **ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go):\\n   - Implements exponential backoff: baseDelay * 2^(num-failures)\\n   - Type: TypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter[T] with failuresLock and failures map\\n   - Key methods: When(item T) time.Duration, NumRequeues(item T) int, Forget(item T)\\n   - Constructor: NewTypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter(baseDelay, maxDelay time.Duration)\\n   - Default usage: 5ms base delay, 1000s max delay in DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter\\n\\n3. **BucketRateLimiter** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go):\\n   - Wraps golang.org/x/time/rate.Limiter\\n   - Type: TypedBucketRateLimiter[T] containing *rate.Limiter\\n   - Token bucket algorithm: 10 QPS, 100 bucket size (default)\\n   - Methods: When(item T) time.Duration, NumRequeues(item T) int, Forget(item T)\\n   - Used in DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter as the overall rate limiter\\n\\n4. **Base Queue Interface** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/queue.go):\\n   - TypedInterface[T] defines: Add(item T), Get() (item T, shutdown bool), Done(item T)\\n   - Implementation: Typed[T] struct with queue, dirty set, processing set\\n   - Key design: dirty set tracks items needing processing, processing set tracks in-flight items\\n   - Get() retrieves items and marks as processing, Done() moves from processing and re-adds if dirty\\n\\n5. **Delaying Queue** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/delaying_queue.go):\\n   - TypedDelayingInterface[T] extends TypedInterface[T]\\n   - Key method: AddAfter(item T, duration time.Duration)\\n   - Implementation: delayingType[T] with priority queue for delayed items\\n   - Automatic re-enqueuing after delay via waitingLoop goroutine\\n\\n**Controller Reconciliation Loop Pattern:**\\n\\nControllers use the work queue with the following pattern (exemplified by deployment_controller.go):\\n\\n1. **Initialization**: queue := workqueue.NewTypedRateLimitingQueue(workqueue.DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter[string]())\\n\\n2. **Run() method** (pkg/controller/deployment/deployment_controller.go lines 162-185):\\n   - Starts worker goroutines: for i := 0; i < workers; i++ { go wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, dc.worker, time.Second) }\\n   - Defers queue.ShutDown()\\n   - Workers run indefinitely until context is done\\n\\n3. **worker() method** (lines 482-485): for dc.processNextWorkItem(ctx) { }\\n\\n4. **processNextWorkItem() method** (lines 487-498):\\n   - Gets item: key, quit := dc.queue.Get()\\n   - Defers: dc.queue.Done(key)\\n   - Calls sync handler (syncDeployment)\\n   - Handles errors via dc.handleErr()\\n   - Returns false if quit=true, else true for next iteration\\n\\n5. **Error handling** (lines 500-520):\\n   - On success: dc.queue.Forget(key)\\n   - On error with retries available: dc.queue.AddRateLimited(key)\\n   - After maxRetries exceeded: dc.queue.Forget(key)\\n   - maxRetries typically 15, resulting in exponential backoff from 5ms to 82s\\n\\n**Example Controller Pattern:**\\n\\nThe staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/examples/workqueue/main.go file provides a complete example showing:\\n- Queue creation with DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter\\n- Controller struct with TypedRateLimitingInterface[string]\\n- processNextItem() method with Get/Done pattern\\n- Proper error handling with AddRateLimited and Forget calls\\n- Integration with informer-based event handlers that call queue.Add(key)\\n\\n**Rate Limiter Composition:**\\n\\nDefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter combines two limiters via TypedMaxOfRateLimiter:\\n1. The core implementation is located in staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/, which is mirrored in the client-go--v0.32.0 repository.\\n\\n**Core Interfaces and Implementations:**\\n\\n1. **RateLimitingInterface** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/rate_limiting_queue.go):\\n   - Defines TypedRateLimitingInterface[T] which extends TypedDelayingInterface[T]\\n   - Key methods: AddRateLimited(item T), Forget(item T), NumRequeues(item T)\\n   - Implementation: rateLimitingType[T] struct wraps a TypedDelayingInterface and a TypedRateLimiter\\n   - Factory functions: NewRateLimitingQueue, NewTypedRateLimitingQueue, NewTypedRateLimitingQueueWithConfig\\n\\n2. **ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go):\\n   - Implements exponential backoff: baseDelay * 2^(num-failures)\\n   - Type: TypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter[T] with failuresLock and failures map\\n   - Key methods: When(item T) time.Duration, NumRequeues(item T) int, Forget(item T)\\n   - Constructor: NewTypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter(baseDelay, maxDelay time.Duration)\\n   - Default usage: 5ms base delay, 1000s max delay in DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter\\n\\n3. **BucketRateLimiter** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go):\\n   - Wraps golang.org/x/time/rate.Limiter\\n   - Type: TypedBucketRateLimiter[T] containing *rate.Limiter\\n   - Token bucket algorithm: 10 QPS, 100 bucket size (default)\\n   - Methods: When(item T) time.Duration, NumRequeues(item T) int, Forget(item T)\\n   - Used in DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter as the overall rate limiter\\n\\n4. **Base Queue Interface** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/queue.go):\\n   - TypedInterface[T] defines: Add(item T), Get() (item T, shutdown bool), Done(item T)\\n   - Implementation: Typed[T] struct with queue, dirty set, processing set\\n   - Key design: dirty set tracks items needing processing, processing set tracks in-flight items\\n   - Get() retrieves items and marks as processing, Done() moves from processing and re-adds if dirty\\n\\n5. **Delaying Queue** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/util/workqueue/delaying_queue.go):\\n   - TypedDelayingInterface[T] extends TypedInterface[T]\\n   - Key method: AddAfter(item T, duration time.Duration)\\n   - Implementation: delayingType[T] with priority queue for delayed items\\n   - Automatic re-enqueuing after delay via waitingLoop goroutine\\n\\n**Controller Reconciliation Loop Pattern:**\\n\\nControllers use the work queue with the following pattern (exemplified by deployment_controller.go):\\n\\n1. **Initialization**: queue := workqueue.NewTypedRateLimitingQueue(workqueue.DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter[string]())\\n\\n2. **Run() method** (pkg/controller/deployment/deployment_controller.go lines 162-185):\\n   - Starts worker goroutines: for i := 0; i < workers; i++ { go wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, dc.worker, time.Second) }\\n   - Defers queue.ShutDown()\\n   - Workers run indefinitely until context is done\\n\\n3. **worker() method** (lines 482-485): for dc.processNextWorkItem(ctx) { }\\n\\n4. **processNextWorkItem() method** (lines 487-498):\\n   - Gets item: key, quit := dc.queue.Get()\\n   - Defers: dc.queue.Done(key)\\n   - Calls sync handler (syncDeployment)\\n   - Handles errors via dc.handleErr()\\n   - Returns false if quit=true, else true for next iteration\\n\\n5. **Error handling** (lines 500-520):\\n   - On success: dc.queue.Forget(key)\\n   - On error with retries available: dc.queue.AddRateLimited(key)\\n   - After maxRetries exceeded: dc.queue.Forget(key)\\n   - maxRetries typically 15, resulting in exponential backoff from 5ms to 82s\\n\\n**Example Controller Pattern:**\\n\\nThe staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/examples/workqueue/main.go file provides a complete example showing:\\n- Queue creation with DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter\\n- Controller struct with TypedRateLimitingInterface[string]\\n- processNextItem() method with Get/Done pattern\\n- Proper error handling with AddRateLimited and Forget calls\\n- Integration with informer-based event handlers that call queue.Add(key)\\n\\n**Rate Limiter Composition:**\\n\\nDefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter combines two limiters via TypedMaxOfRateLimiter:\\n1. ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter: per-item exponential backoff\\n2. BucketRateLimiter: overall system rate limiting (10 QPS)\\n\\nThe limiting function returns the maximum delay from both limiters, ensuring both are respected.\\n\\n**Actual Implementations in Controllers:**\\n\\nNumerous Kubernetes controllers use this pattern, including:\\n- DeploymentController (pkg/controller/deployment/deployment_controller.go)\\n- JobController (pkg/controller/job/job_controller.go)\\n- DaemonSetController (pkg/controller/daemon/daemon_controller.go)\\n- ReplicaSetController (pkg/controller/replicaset/replica_set.go)\\n- NamespaceController (pkg/controller/namespace/namespace_controller.go)\\n- StatefulSetController (pkg/controller/statefulset/stateful_set.go)\\n- EndpointController (pkg/controller/endpoint/endpoints_controller.go)\\n- EndpointSliceController (pkg/controller/endpointslice/endpointslice_controller.go)\\n- GarbageCollectorController (pkg/controller/garbagecollector/garbagecollector.go)\\n- CertificateController (pkg/controller/certificates/certificate_controller.go)\\n- CronjobControllerV2 (pkg/controller/cronjob/cronjob_controllerv2.go)\\n- And many others in staging/src/k8s.io/ (cloud-provider, kube-aggregator, etc.)\\n\\nAll follow the same core pattern: initialize with RateLimitingQueue, run workers that Get/Done items, and use AddRateLimited for failures.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
